  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This daemon acts as a name server on all hosts involved in\n      distributed Erlang computations. When an Erlang node starts,\n      the node has a name and it obtains an address from the host\n      OS kernel. The name and address are sent to the\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"epmd">>]},
    <<" daemon running on the local host.\n      In a TCP/IP environment, the address consists\n      of the IP address and a port number. The node name is\n      an atom on the form of ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Name@Node">>]},
    <<".\n      The job of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"epmd">>]},
    <<" daemon is to keep track of which\n      node name listens on which address. Hence, ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"epmd">>]},
    <<" maps\n      symbolic node names to machine addresses.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The TCP/IP ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"epmd">>]},
    <<" daemon only keeps track of\n      the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Name">>]},
    <<" (first) part of an Erlang node name. The ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Host">>]},
    <<"\n      part (whatever is after the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"@">>]},
    <<") is implicit in the\n      node name where the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"epmd">>]},
    <<" daemon was contacted,\n      as is the IP address where the Erlang node can be\n      reached. Consistent and correct TCP naming services are\n      therefore required for an Erlang network to function\n      correctly.">>]},

  {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"WARNING">>}],[]},

    {<<"div">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"content">>}],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"p">>,[],
         [{<<"strong">>,[],
           [<<"Use this functionality with extreme care.">>]}]},
        {<<"p">>,[],
         [<<"A driver callback is executed as a direct extension of the\n        native code of the VM. Execution is not made in a safe environment.\n        The VM ">>,
          {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"cannot">>]},
          <<" provide the same services as provided when\n        executing Erlang code, such as pre-emptive scheduling or memory\n        protection. If the driver callback function does not behave well,\n        the whole VM will misbehave.">>]},
        {<<"ul">>,[],
         [{<<"li">>,[],
           [{<<"p">>,[],
             [<<"A driver callback that crash will crash the whole VM.">>]}]},
          {<<"li">>,[],
           [{<<"p">>,[],
             [<<"An erroneously implemented driver callback can cause a VM\n            internal state inconsistency, which can cause a crash of the VM,\n            or miscellaneous misbehaviors of the VM at any point after the\n            call to the driver callback.">>]}]},
          {<<"li">>,[],
           [{<<"p">>,[],
             [<<"A driver callback doing\n            ">>,
              {<<"span">>,
               [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
               [{<<"a">>,
                 [{<<"href">>,<<"#lengthy_work">>}],
                 [<<"lengthy work">>]}]},
              <<" before\n            returning degrades responsiveness of the VM and can cause\n            miscellaneous strange behaviors. Such strange behaviors\n            include, but are not limited to, extreme memory usage and bad\n            load balancing between schedulers. Strange behaviors that can\n            occur because of lengthy work can also vary between Erlang/OTP\n            releases.">>]}]}]}]}]}]},

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"smp_support">>}],[]},
    <<"In the runtime system with\n      SMP support, drivers are locked either on driver level\n      or port level (driver instance level). By default\n      driver level locking will be used, that is, only one emulator thread\n      will execute code in the driver at a time. If port level locking\n      is used, multiple emulator threads can execute code in the driver\n      at the same time. Only one thread at a time will call\n      driver callbacks corresponding to the same port, though.\n      To enable port level locking, set the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
     [<<"ERL_DRV_FLAG_USE_PORT_LOCKING">>]},
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"driver_entry.html#driver_flags">>}],
       [<<"driver flag">>]}]},
    <<" in\n      the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"driver_entry.html">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"driver_entry">>]}]}]},
    <<"\n      used by the driver. When port level locking is used,\n      the driver writer is responsible for synchronizing all accesses\n      to data shared by the ports (driver instances).">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Most drivers written before the runtime system with SMP\n      support existed can run in the runtime system\n      with SMP support, without being rewritten, if driver\n      level locking is used.">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"note">>}],
   [{<<"div">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"label">>}],[<<"Note">>]},
    {<<"div">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"content">>}],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"p">>,[],
         [<<"It is assumed that drivers do not access other drivers. If\n        drivers access each other, they must provide their own\n        mechanism for thread-safe synchronization. Such \"inter-driver\n        communication\" is strongly discouraged.">>]}]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Previously, in the runtime system without SMP support,\n      specific driver callbacks were always called from the same\n      thread. This is ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"not">>]},
    <<" the case in the runtime system\n      with SMP support. Regardless of locking scheme used, calls\n      to driver callbacks can be made from different threads. For example,\n      two consecutive calls to exactly the same callback for exactly\n      the same port can be made from two different threads. This\n      is for ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"most">>]},
    <<" drivers not a problem, but it can be.\n      Drivers that depend on all callbacks that are called in the\n      same thread, ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"must">>]},
    <<" be rewritten before they are used\n      in the runtime system with SMP support.">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"note">>}],

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Most functions in this API are ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"not">>]},
    <<" thread-safe, that is,\n      they ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"cannot">>]},
    <<" be called from any thread. Functions\n      that are not documented as thread-safe can only be called from\n      driver callbacks or function calls descending from a driver\n      callback call. This, however, is not a problem for any\n      function in this API, as the emulator has control over\n      these threads.">>]},

   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"lengthy_work">>}],[]},

    <<" text at\n      the beginning of this section, it is of vital importance that a driver\n      callback returns relatively fast. It is difficult to give an exact\n      maximum amount of time that a driver callback is allowed to work, but\n      usually a well-behaving driver callback is to return within 1 millisecond.\n      This can be achieved using different approaches.\n      If you have full control over the code to execute in the driver\n      callback, the best approach is to divide the work into multiple chunks of\n      work, and trigger multiple calls to the\n      ">>,

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"A NIF library contains native implementation of some functions\n      of an Erlang module. The native implemented functions (NIFs) are\n      called like any other functions without any difference to the\n      caller. Each NIF must have an implementation in Erlang that\n      is invoked if the function is called before the NIF library\n      is successfully loaded. A typical such stub implementation\n      is to throw an exception. But it can also be used as a fallback\n      implementation if the NIF library is not implemented for some\n      architecture.">>]},

       [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
       [<<"erl -mode interactive">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"The modes are as follows:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"In embedded mode, all code is loaded during system startup\n          according to the boot script. (Code can also be loaded later\n          by explicitly ordering the code server to do so).">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"In interactive mode, which is default, only some code is loaded\n\t  during system startup, basically the modules needed by the runtime\n          system. Other code is dynamically loaded when first\n          referenced. When a call to a function in a certain module is\n          made, and the module is not loaded, the code server searches\n          for and tries to load the module.">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"To prevent accidentally reloading of modules affecting the Erlang\n      runtime system, directories ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"kernel">>]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"stdlib">>]},
    <<",\n      and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"compiler">>]},
    <<" are considered ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"sticky">>]},
    <<". This\n      means that the system issues a warning and rejects the request if\n      a user tries to reload a module residing in any of them.\n      The feature can be disabled by using command-line flag\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"-nostick">>]},
    <<".">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"disk_log">>]},
    <<" is a disk-based term logger that enables\n      efficient logging of items on files.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"Two types of logs are supported:">>]},
  {<<"dl">>,[],
   [{<<"dt">>,[],[{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"halt logs">>]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Appends items to a single file, which size can\n\tbe limited by the disk log module.">>]}]},
    {<<"dt">>,[],[{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"wrap logs">>]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Uses a sequence of wrap log files of limited size. As a\n\twrap log file is filled up, further items are logged on to the next\n\tfile in the sequence, starting all over with the first file when\n\tthe last file is filled up.">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"For efficiency reasons, items are always written to files as binaries.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"Two formats of the log files are supported:">>]},
  {<<"dl">>,[],
   [{<<"dt">>,[],[{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"internal format">>]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Supports automatic repair of log files that are not\n\tproperly closed and enables efficient reading of logged items in\n\t">>,
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"chunks">>]},
        <<" using a set of functions defined in this module.\n\tThis is the only way to read internally formatted logs.\n\tAn item logged to an internally formatted log must not occupy more\n\tthan 4 GB of disk space (the size must fit in 4 bytes).">>]}]},
    {<<"dt">>,[],[{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"external format">>]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Leaves it up to the user to read the logged deep byte lists.\n\tThe disk log module cannot repair externally formatted logs.">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"For each open disk log, one process handles requests\n      made to the disk log. This process is created when\n      ">>,

     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],

       [{<<"href">>,<<"#open-1">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"open/1">>]}]}]},

    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"owner">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],

    <<" of a driver.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"In the basic scenario, each user loads the driver before\n      starting to use it and unloads the driver when done.\n      The reference counting keeps track of\n      processes and the number of loads by each process. This way\n      the driver is only unloaded when no one wants it (it has no user).\n      The driver also keeps track of ports that are\n      opened to it. This enables delay of unloading until all\n      ports are closed, or killing of all ports that use the driver when\n      it is unloaded.">>]},
  {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"scenarios">>}],[]},
  {<<"p">>,[],

   [{<<"dt">>,[],

    {<<"dd">>,[],

         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
        <<" of the driver loads\n          it when needed and unloads it when no longer needed.\n          The driver is always reference counted and as long as a\n          process keeping the driver loaded is still alive, the driver\n          is present in the system.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Each ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
        <<" of the driver\n          use ">>,
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"literally">>]},
        <<" the same pathname for the driver when\n          demanding load, but the\n\t  ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"users">>]}]},
        <<" are not concerned\n          with if the driver is already loaded from the file system or\n          if the object code must be loaded from file system.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The following two pairs of functions support this scenario:">>]},
      {<<"dl">>,[],
       [{<<"dt">>,[],
         [{<<"strong">>,[],[{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"load/2 and unload/1">>]}]}]},
        {<<"dd">>,[],
         [{<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"When using the ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"load/unload">>]},
            <<" interfaces, the\n              driver is not unloaded until the\n              ">>,
            {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"last port">>]},
            <<" using the driver is closed. Function\n              ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"unload/1">>]},
            <<" can return immediately, as the\n\t      ">>,
            {<<"span">>,
             [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
             [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"users">>]}]},
            <<"\n\t      have no interrest in when the unloading occurs. The\n              driver is unloaded when no one needs it any longer.">>]},
          {<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"If a process having the driver loaded dies, it has\n              the same effect as if unloading is done.">>]},
          {<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"When loading, function ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"load/2">>]},
            <<" returns\n              ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ok">>]},
            <<" when any instance of the driver is\n              present. Thus, if a driver is waiting to get unloaded\n              (because of open ports), it simply changes state to no\n              longer need unloading.">>]}]},
        {<<"dt">>,[],
         [{<<"strong">>,[],
           [{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"load_driver/2 and unload_driver/1">>]}]}]},
        {<<"dd">>,[],
         [{<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"These interfaces are intended to be used when it is considered an\n              error that ports are open to a driver that no\n\t      ">>,
            {<<"span">>,
             [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
             [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
            <<"\n              has loaded. The ports that are still open when the\n              last ">>,
            {<<"span">>,
             [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
             [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
            <<" calls\n              ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"unload_driver/1">>]},
            <<" or when the last process having the\n              driver loaded dies, are killed with reason\n              ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"driver_unloaded">>]},
            <<".">>]},
          {<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"The function names ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"load_driver">>]},
            <<" and\n              ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"unload_driver">>]},
            <<" are kept for backward\n              compatibility.">>]}]}]}]},
    {<<"dt">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],
       [{<<"strong">>,[],
         [<<"Loading and Reloading for Code Replacement">>]}]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"This scenario can occur if the driver code needs\n          replacement during operation of the Erlang\n          emulator. Implementing driver code replacement is a little\n          more tedious than Beam code replacement, as one driver\n          cannot be loaded as both \"old\" and \"new\" code. All\n\t  ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"users">>]}]},
        <<" of a driver must have it\n          closed (no open ports) before the old code can be unloaded\n          and the new code can be loaded.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The unloading/loading is done as one atomic\n          operation, blocking all processes in the system from using\n          the driver in question while in progress.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The preferred way to do driver code replacement is to let\n          ">>,
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"one single process">>]},
        <<" keep track of the driver. When\n          the process starts, the driver is loaded. When replacement\n          is required, the driver is reloaded. Unload is probably never\n          done, or done when the process exits. If more than one\n\t  ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
        <<" has a driver\n\t  loaded when code replacement is demanded, the replacement cannot\n\t  occur until the last \"other\"\n\t  ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
        <<" has\n          unloaded the driver.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Demanding reload when a reload is already in progress is\n          always an error. Using the high-level functions, it is also\n          an error to demand reloading when more than one\n\t  ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
        <<" has the driver loaded.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"To simplify driver replacement, avoid designing your system so\n          that more than one\n\t  ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"user">>]}]},
        <<" has the driver loaded.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The two functions for reloading drivers are to be used\n          together with corresponding load functions to support the two\n          different behaviors concerning open ports:">>]},
      {<<"dl">>,[],
       [{<<"dt">>,[],
         [{<<"strong">>,[],[{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"load/2 and reload/2">>]}]}]},
        {<<"dd">>,[],
         [{<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"This pair of functions is used when reloading is to be\n              done after the last open port to the driver is\n              closed.">>]},
          {<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"As ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"reload/2">>]},
            <<" waits for the reloading to\n              occur, a misbehaving process keeping open ports to\n              the driver (or keeping the driver loaded) can cause\n              infinite waiting for reload. Time-outs must be provided\n              outside of the process demanding the reload or by using\n              the low-level interface\n\t      ">>,
            {<<"span">>,
             [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
             [{<<"a">>,
               [{<<"href">>,<<"#try_load-3">>}],
               [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"try_load/3">>]}]}]},
            <<"\n\t      in combination with driver monitors.">>]}]},
        {<<"dt">>,[],
         [{<<"strong">>,[],
           [{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"load_driver/2 and reload_driver/2">>]}]}]},
        {<<"dd">>,[],
         [{<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"This pair of functions are used when open ports to\n              the driver are to be killed with reason\n              ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"driver_unloaded">>]},
            <<" to allow for new driver code to\n              get loaded.">>]},
          {<<"p">>,[],
           [<<"However, if another process has the driver loaded,\n              calling ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"reload_driver">>]},
            <<" returns error code\n              ">>,
            {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"pending_process">>]},
            <<". As stated earlier,\n              the recommended design is to not allow other\n\t      ">>,
            {<<"span">>,
             [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
             [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#users">>}],[<<"users">>]}]},
            <<" than the \"driver\n              reloader\" to demand loading of the driver in question.">>]}]}]}]}]}],

   [<<"These record definitions use the \"new\" spelling 'adaptation',\n      not the deprecated 'adaption', regardless of which\n      spelling the underlying C API uses.">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module provides functions for communicating\n      with sockets using the TCP/IP protocol.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The following code fragment is a simple example of\n      a client connecting to a server at port 5678, transferring a\n      binary, and closing the connection:">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"\nclient() ->\n    SomeHostInNet = \"localhost\", % to make it runnable on one machine\n    {ok, Sock} = gen_tcp:connect(SomeHostInNet, 5678, \n                                 [binary, {packet, 0}]),\n    ok = gen_tcp:send(Sock, \"Some Data\"),\n    ok = gen_tcp:close(Sock).">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"At the other end, a server is listening on port 5678, accepts\n      the connection, and receives the binary:">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"\nserver() ->\n    {ok, LSock} = gen_tcp:listen(5678, [binary, {packet, 0}, \n                                        {active, false}]),\n    {ok, Sock} = gen_tcp:accept(LSock),\n    {ok, Bin} = do_recv(Sock, []),\n    ok = gen_tcp:close(Sock),\n    Bin.\n\ndo_recv(Sock, Bs) ->\n    case gen_tcp:recv(Sock, 0) of\n        {ok, B} ->\n            do_recv(Sock, [Bs, B]);\n        {error, closed} ->\n            {ok, list_to_binary(Bs)}\n    end.">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"For more examples, see section\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#examples">>}],[<<"Examples">>]}]},
    <<".">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module provides functions for communicating\n      with sockets using the UDP protocol.">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],[<<"This module consists of the following services:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],[<<"Registration of global names">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],[<<"Global locks">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],[<<"Maintenance of the fully connected network">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"These services are controlled through the process\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"global_name_server">>]},
    <<" that exists on every node. The global\n      name server starts automatically when a node is started.\n      With the term ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"global">>]},
    <<" is meant over a system consisting\n      of many Erlang nodes.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The ability to globally register names is a central concept in\n      the programming of distributed Erlang systems. In this module,\n      the equivalent of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"register/2">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"whereis/1">>]},
    <<"\n      BIFs (for local name registration) are provided, but for a\n      network of Erlang nodes. A registered name is an alias for a\n      process identifier (pid). The global name server monitors\n      globally registered pids. If a process terminates, the name is\n      also globally unregistered.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The registered names are stored in replica global name tables on\n      every node. There is no central storage point. Thus,\n      the translation of a name to a pid is fast, as it is always done\n      locally. For any action resulting in a change to the global name table,\n      all tables on other nodes are automatically updated.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Global locks have lock identities and are set on a specific\n      resource. For example, the specified resource can be a pid.\n      When a global lock is set, access to the locked resource is\n      denied for all resources other than the lock requester.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Both the registration and lock services are atomic.\n      All nodes involved in these actions have the same view of\n      the information.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The global name server also performs the critical task of\n      continuously monitoring changes in node configuration. If a node\n      that runs a globally registered process goes down, the name\n      is globally unregistered. To this end, the global name\n      server subscribes to ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"nodeup">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"nodedown">>]},
    <<" messages\n      sent from module ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"net_kernel">>]},
    <<". Relevant Kernel\n      application variables in this context are ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"net_setuptime">>]},
    <<",\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"net_ticktime">>]},
    <<", and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"dist_auto_connect">>]},
    <<". See also\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"kernel_app.html#net_setuptime">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"kernel(6)">>]}]}]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The name server also maintains a fully connected network. For\n      example, if node ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N1">>]},
    <<" connects to node ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N2">>]},
    <<" (which is\n      already connected to ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N3">>]},
    <<"), the global name servers on the\n      nodes ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N1">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N3">>]},
    <<" ensure that also ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N1">>]},
    <<"\n      and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N3">>]},
    <<" are connected. If this is not desired,\n      command-line flag ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"-connect_all false">>]},
    <<" can be used (see also\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"erl.html#connect_all">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl(1)">>]}]}]},
    <<").\n      In this case, the name registration service cannot be used, but the\n      lock mechanism still works.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If the global name server fails to connect nodes (">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N1">>]},
    <<" and\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"N3">>]},
    <<" in the example), a warning event is sent to the\n      error logger. The presence of such an event does not exclude the\n      nodes to connect later (you can, for\n      example, try command ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
     [<<"rpc:call(N1, net_adm, ping, [N2])">>]},
    <<" in\n      the Erlang shell), but it indicates a network problem.">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"note">>}],
   [{<<"div">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"label">>}],[<<"Note">>]},
    {<<"div">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"content">>}],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"p">>,[],
         [<<"If the fully connected network is not set up properly, try\n        first to increase the value of ">>,
          {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"net_setuptime">>]},
          <<".">>]}]}]}]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module makes it possible to partition the nodes of a\n      system into ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"global groups">>]},
    <<". Each global group has its own\n      global namespace, see ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"global.html">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"global(3)">>]}]}]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The main advantage of dividing systems into global groups is that\n      the background load decreases while the number of nodes to be\n      updated is reduced when manipulating globally registered names.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The Kernel configuration parameter ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"global_groups">>]},

     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"kernel_app.html#global_groups">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"kernel(6)">>]}]}]},

    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"config.html">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"config(4)">>]}]}]},
    <<"):">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"\n{global_groups, [GroupTuple :: group_tuple()]}">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"For the processes and nodes to run smoothly using the global\n      group functionality, the following criteria must be met:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This modules contains the interface to the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"heart">>]},
    <<" process.\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"heart">>]},
    <<" sends periodic heartbeats to an external port\n      program, which is also named ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"heart">>]},
    <<". The purpose of\n      the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"heart">>]},
    <<" port program is to check that the Erlang runtime system\n      it is supervising is still running. If the port program has not\n      received any heartbeats within ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"HEART_BEAT_TIMEOUT">>]},
    <<" seconds\n      (defaults to 60 seconds), the system can be rebooted. Also, if\n      the system is equipped with a hardware watchdog timer and is\n      running Solaris, the watchdog can be used to supervise the entire\n      system.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"An Erlang runtime system to be monitored by a heart program\n      is to be started with command-line flag ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"-heart">>]},
    <<" (see\n      also ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"erl.html">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl(1)">>]}]}]},
    <<").\n      The ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"heart">>]},
    <<" process is then started automatically:">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"\n% ">>,
      {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],[<<"erl -heart ...">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If the system is to be rebooted because of missing heartbeats,\n      or a terminated Erlang runtime system, environment variable\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"HEART_COMMAND">>]},
    <<" must be set before the system is started.\n      If this variable is not set, a warning text is printed but\n      the system does not reboot. However, if the hardware watchdog is\n      used, it still triggers a reboot ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"HEART_BEAT_BOOT_DELAY">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The release package can be ">>,

    <<".\n      The currently used version of the release is then upgraded or\n      downgraded to the specified version by evaluating the instructions\n      in the ">>,

    <<". When a release is removed, all files\n      belonging to that release only are deleted.">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The release handler process is a locally registered process on\n      each node. When a release is installed in a distributed system,\n      the release handler on each node must be called. The release\n      installation can be synchronized between nodes. From an operator\n      view, it can be unsatisfactory to specify each node. The aim is\n      to install one release package in the system, no matter how many\n      nodes there are. It is recommended that\n      software management functions are written that take care of\n      this problem. Such a function can have knowledge of the system\n      architecture, so it can contact each individual release handler\n      to install the package.">>]},

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Functional, extendible arrays. Arrays can have fixed size, or can grow\n      automatically as needed. A default value is used for entries that have not\n      been explicitly set.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Arrays uses ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"zero">>]},
    <<"-based indexing. This is a deliberate design\n      choice and differs from other Erlang data structures, for example,\n      tuples.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Unless specified by the user when the array is created, the default\n      value is the atom ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"undefined">>]},
    <<". There is no difference between an\n      unset entry and an entry that has been explicitly set to the same value\n      as the default one (compare\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"#reset-2">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"reset/2">>]}]}]},
    <<"). If you need to\n      differentiate between unset and set entries, ensure that the default value\n      cannot be confused with the values of set entries.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The array never shrinks automatically. If an index ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"I">>]},
    <<" has been used\n      to set an entry successfully, all indices in the range [0,">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"I">>]},
    <<"] stay\n      accessible unless the array size is explicitly changed by calling\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"#resize-2">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"resize/2">>]}]}]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Examples:">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Create a fixed-size array with entries 0-9 set to ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"undefined">>]},
    <<":">>]},

   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"\nA0 = array:new(10).\n10 = array:size(A0).">>]}]},

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The include file ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"assert.hrl">>]},
    <<" provides macros for inserting\n      assertions in your program code.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],

   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"\n-include_lib(\"stdlib/include/assert.hrl\").">>]}]},

   [<<"When an assertion succeeds, the assert macro yields the atom ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ok">>]},
    <<".\n      When an assertion fails, an exception of type ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"error">>]},
    <<" is generated.\n      The associated error term has the form ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{Macro, Info}">>]},
    <<". ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Macro">>]},

    <<". ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Info">>]},
    <<" is a list\n      of tagged values, such as ">>,

   [<<"For example, using ">>,

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module provides a term storage on file. The\n      stored terms, in this module called ">>,

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module is used by the Mnesia application, and is provided\n      \"as is\" for users who are interested in efficient storage of Erlang\n      terms on disk only. If larger\n      tables are needed, table fragmentation in Mnesia can be used.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"Three types of Dets tables exist:">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Dets tables must be opened before they can be updated or read,\n      and when finished they must be properly closed. If a table is not\n      properly closed, Dets automatically repairs the table.\n      This can take a substantial time if the table is large. A Dets\n      table is closed when the process which opened the table\n      terminates. If many Erlang processes (users) open the same Dets\n      table, they share the table. The table is properly closed\n      when all users have either terminated or closed the table. Dets\n      tables are not properly closed if the Erlang runtime system\n      terminates abnormally.">>]},

        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"labeled digraph">>]},
        <<", and the\n          information attached to a vertex or an edge is called a\n          ">>,
        {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"label">>}],[]},
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"label">>]},
        <<".">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"An edge e = (v, w) is said to\n          ">>,
        {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"emanate">>}],[]},
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"emanate">>]},
        <<" from vertex v and to\n          be ">>,
        {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"incident">>}],[]},
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"incident">>]},
        <<" on vertex w.">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],

        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"path">>]},
        <<" P from v[1] to v[k]\n          in a digraph (V, E) is a non-empty sequence\n          v[1], v[2], ..., v[k] of vertices in V such that\n          there is an edge (v[i],v[i+1]) in E for\n          1 <= i < k.">>]}]},

        {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"acyclic_digraph">>}],[]},
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"acyclic digraph">>]},
        <<"\n          is a digraph without cycles.">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"A ">>,
        {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"depth_first_traversal">>}],[]},
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"depth-first\n          traversal">>]},
        <<" of a directed digraph can be viewed as a process\n          that visits all vertices of the digraph. Initially, all vertices\n          are marked as unvisited. The traversal starts with an\n          arbitrarily chosen vertex, which is marked as visited, and\n          follows an edge to an unmarked vertex, marking that vertex. The\n          search then proceeds from that vertex in the same fashion, until\n          there is no edge leading to an unvisited vertex. At that point\n          the process backtracks, and the traversal continues as long as\n          there are unexamined edges. If unvisited vertices remain\n          when all edges from the first vertex have been examined, some\n          so far unvisited vertex is chosen, and the process is repeated.">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"A ">>,
        {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"partial_ordering">>}],[]},
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"partial ordering">>]},
        <<"\n          of a set S is a transitive, antisymmetric, and reflexive relation\n          between the objects of S.">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],

        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"digraph">>]},

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module is an interface to the Erlang built-in term storage\n      BIFs. These provide the ability to store very large quantities of\n      data in an Erlang runtime system, and to have constant access\n      time to the data. (In the case of ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ordered_set">>]},
    <<", see below,\n      access time is proportional to the logarithm of the number of\n      stored objects.)">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Data is organized as a set of dynamic tables, which can store\n      tuples. Each table is created by a process. When the process\n      terminates, the table is automatically destroyed. Every table has\n      access rights set at creation.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Tables are divided into four different types, ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"set">>]},
    <<",\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ordered_set">>]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"bag">>]},
    <<", and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"duplicate_bag">>]},
    <<".\n      A ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"set">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ordered_set">>]},
    <<" table can only have one object\n      associated with each key. A ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"bag">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"duplicate_bag">>]},
    <<" table can\n      have many objects associated with each key.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The number of tables stored at one Erlang node is limited.\n      The current default limit is about 1400 tables. The upper\n      limit can be increased by setting environment variable\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ERL_MAX_ETS_TABLES">>]},
    <<" before starting the Erlang runtime\n      system (that is, with option ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"-env">>]},
    <<" to\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl">>]},
    <<"/">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"werl">>]},
    <<"). The actual limit can be slightly higher\n      than the one specified, but never lower.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Notice that there is no automatic garbage collection for tables.\n      Even if there are no references to a table from any process, it\n      is not automatically destroyed unless the owner process\n      terminates. To destroy a table explicitly, use function\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"#delete-1">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"delete/1">>]}]}]},

     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"#heir">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"heir">>]}]}]},
    <<" or call\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,
       [{<<"href">>,<<"#give_away-3">>}],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"give_away/3">>]}]}]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"Some implementation details:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"In the current implementation, every object insert and\n       look-up operation results in a copy of the object.">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'$end_of_table'">>]},
        <<" is not to be used as a key, as\n       this atom is used to mark the end of the table when using functions\n       ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,
           [{<<"href">>,<<"#first-1">>}],
           [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"first/1">>]}]}]},
        <<" and\n       ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
         [{<<"a">>,
           [{<<"href">>,<<"#next-2">>}],
           [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"next/2">>]}]}]},
        <<".">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Notice the subtle difference between\n      ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"matching">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"comparing equal">>]},
    <<", which is\n      demonstrated by table types ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"set">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ordered_set">>]},
    <<":">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Two Erlang terms ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"match">>]},
        <<" if they are of\n          the same type and have the same value, so that ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"1">>]},
        <<" matches\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"1">>]},
        <<", but not ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"1.0">>]},

     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Two Erlang terms ">>,

        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"1">>]},

        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"1">>]},

        <<".">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ordered_set">>]},
        <<" works on the ">>,
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Erlang term order">>]},
        <<" and\n          no defined order exists between an ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"integer()">>]},
        <<" and a\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"float()">>]},
        <<" that extends to the same value. Hence the key\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"1">>]},
        <<" and the key ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"1.0">>]},
        <<" are regarded as equal in an\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ordered_set">>]},
        <<" table.">>]}]}]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module contains functions for sorting terms on files, merging\n      already sorted files, and checking files for sortedness. Chunks\n      containing binary terms are read from a sequence of files, sorted\n      internally in memory and written on temporary files, which are\n      merged producing one sorted file as output. Merging is provided\n      as an optimization; it is faster when the files are already\n      sorted, but it always works to sort instead of merge.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"On a file, a term is represented by a header and a binary. Two\n      options define the format of terms on files:">>]},
  {<<"dl">>,[],
   [{<<"dt">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
         [<<"{header, HeaderLength}">>]}]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"HeaderLength">>]},
        <<" determines the\n          number of bytes preceding each binary and containing the\n          length of the binary in bytes. Defaults to 4. The order of the\n          header bytes is defined as follows: if ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"B">>]},
        <<" is a binary\n          containing a header only, size ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Size">>]},
        <<" of the binary\n          is calculated as\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
         [<<"<<Size:HeaderLength/unit:8>> = B">>]},
        <<".">>]}]},
    {<<"dt">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{format, Format}">>]}]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Option ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Format">>]},
        <<" determines the\n          function that is applied to binaries to create the\n          terms to be sorted. Defaults to\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"binary_term">>]},
        <<", which is equivalent to\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"fun binary_to_term/1">>]},
        <<". Value ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"binary">>]},
        <<" is\n          equivalent to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"fun(X) -> X end">>]},
        <<", which means that the\n          binaries are sorted as they are. This is the fastest\n          format. If ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Format">>]},
        <<" is ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"term">>]},
        <<", ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"io:read/2">>]},
        <<" is\n          called to read terms. In that case, only the default value of\n          option ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"header">>]},
        <<" is allowed.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Option ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"format">>]},
        <<" also determines what is written to the\n          sorted output file: if\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Format">>]},
        <<" is ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"term">>]},
        <<", then ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"io:format/3">>]},
        <<" is called\n          to write each term, otherwise the binary prefixed by a header\n          is written. Notice that the binary written is the same binary\n          that was read; the results of applying function ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Format">>]},
        <<"\n          are thrown away when the terms have been sorted.\n          Reading and writing terms using the ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"io">>]},
        <<" module\n          is much slower than reading and writing binaries.">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"Other options are:">>]},
  {<<"dl">>,[],
   [{<<"dt">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{order, Order}">>]}]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The default is to sort terms in\n          ascending order, but that can be changed by value\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"descending">>]},
        <<" or by specifying an ordering function ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Fun">>]},
        <<".\n          An ordering function is antisymmetric, transitive, and total.\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Fun(A, B)">>]},
        <<" is to return ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"true">>]},
        <<" if ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"A">>]},
        <<"\n          comes before ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"B">>]},
        <<" in the ordering, otherwise ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"false">>]},
        <<".\n          An example of a typical ordering function is less than or equal\n          to, ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"=</2">>]},
        <<". Using an ordering function slows down the sort\n          considerably. Functions ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"keysort">>]},
        <<", ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"keymerge">>]},

        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"keycheck">>]},

    {<<"dt">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
         [<<"{unique, boolean()}">>]}]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"When sorting or merging files,\n           only the first of a sequence of terms that compare equal (">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"==">>]},
        <<")\n           is output if this option is set to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"true">>]},
        <<". Defaults\n           to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"false">>]},
        <<", which implies that all terms that\n           compare equal are output. When checking files for\n           sortedness, a check that no pair of consecutive terms\n           compares equal is done if this option is set to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"true">>]},
        <<".">>]}]},
    {<<"dt">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],

         [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
         [<<"{tmpdir, TempDirectory}">>]}]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The directory where\n           temporary files are put can be chosen explicitly. The\n           default, implied by value ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"\"">>]},
        <<", is to put temporary\n           files on the same directory as the sorted output file. If\n           output is a function (see below), the directory returned by\n           ">>,

        <<"), and a unique integer\n           (">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
         [<<"erlang:unique_integer([positive])">>]},
        <<"). A typical name is\n           ">>,
        {<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
         [<<"fs_mynode@myhost_1763_4711.17">>]},
        <<", where\n           ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"17">>]},
        <<" is a sequence number. Existing files are\n           overwritten. Temporary files are deleted unless some\n           uncaught ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"EXIT">>]},
        <<" signal occurs.">>]}]},
    {<<"dt">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,
         [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
         [<<"{compressed, boolean()}">>]}]}]},
    {<<"dd">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Temporary files and the output file can be compressed. Defaults\n          ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"false">>]},

        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"compressed">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"As an alternative to sorting files, a function of one argument\n      can be specified as input. When called with argument ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"read">>]},
    <<",\n      the function is assumed to return either of the following:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"end_of_input">>]},

        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Fun">>]},
        <<" is a new input\n          function.">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Any other value is immediately returned as value of the current call\n      to ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"sort">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"keysort">>]},
    <<". Each input function is\n      called exactly once. If an error occurs, the last\n      function is called with argument ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"close">>]},
    <<", the reply of\n      which is ignored.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"A function of one argument can be specified as output. The results\n      of sorting or merging the input is collected in a non-empty\n      sequence of variable length lists of binaries or terms depending\n      on the format. The output function is called with one list at a\n      time, and is assumed to return a new output function. Any other\n      return value is immediately returned as value of the current\n      call to the sort or merge function. Each output function is\n      called exactly once. When some output function has been applied\n      to all of the results or an error occurs, the last function is\n      called with argument ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"close">>]},
    <<", and the reply is returned\n      as value of the current call to the sort or merge function.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If a function is specified as input and the last input function\n      returns ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{end_of_input, Value}">>]},
    <<", the function specified as output\n      is called with argument ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{value, Value}">>]},
    <<". This makes it\n      easy to initiate the sequence of output functions with a value\n      calculated by the input functions.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"As an example, consider sorting the terms on a disk log file.\n      A function that reads chunks from the disk log and returns a\n      list of binaries is used as input. The results are collected in\n      a list of terms.">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"\nsort(Log) ->\n    {ok, _} = disk_log:open([{name,Log}, {mode,read_only}]),\n    Input = input(Log, start),\n    Output = output([]),\n    Reply = file_sorter:sort(Input, Output, {format,term}),\n    ok = disk_log:close(Log),\n    Reply.\n\ninput(Log, Cont) ->\n    fun(close) ->\n            ok;\n       (read) ->\n            case disk_log:chunk(Log, Cont) of\n                {error, Reason} ->\n                    {error, Reason};\n                {Cont2, Terms} ->\n                    {Terms, input(Log, Cont2)};\n                {Cont2, Terms, _Badbytes} ->\n                    {Terms, input(Log, Cont2)};\n                eof ->\n                    end_of_input\n            end\n    end.\n\noutput(L) ->\n    fun(close) ->\n            lists:append(lists:reverse(L));\n       (Terms) ->\n            output([Terms | L])\n    end.">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"For more examples of functions as input and output, see\n      the end of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"file_sorter">>]},
    <<" module; the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"term">>]},
    <<"\n      format is implemented with functions.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The possible values of ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Reason">>]},
    <<" returned when an error\n      occurs are:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"bad_object">>]},
        <<", ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{bad_object, FileName}">>]},
        <<" -\n          Applying the format function failed for some binary,\n          or the key(s) could not be extracted from some term.">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],

  {<<"p">>,[],

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module provides a random number generator. The method is attributed\n      to B.A. Wichmann and I.D. Hill in 'An efficient and portable\n      pseudo-random number generator', Journal of Applied\n      Statistics. AS183. 1982. Also Byte March 1987.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The algorithm is a modification of the version attributed\n      to Richard A. O'Keefe in the standard Prolog library.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Every time a random number is requested, a state is used to calculate\n      it, and a new state is produced. The state can either be implicit (kept\n      in the process dictionary) or be an explicit argument and return value.\n      In this implementation, the state (the type ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ran()">>]},
    <<") consists of a\n      tuple of three integers.">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"note">>}],
   [{<<"div">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"label">>}],[<<"Note">>]},
    {<<"div">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"content">>}],
     [{<<"p">>,[],

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module provides operations on finite sets and\n      relations represented as sets. Intuitively, a set is a\n      collection of elements; every element belongs to the set, and\n      the set contains every element.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Given a set A and a sentence S(x), where x is a free variable,\n      a new set B whose elements are exactly those elements of A for\n      which S(x) holds can be formed, this is denoted B =\n      {x in A : S(x)}. Sentences are expressed using\n      the logical operators \"for some\" (or \"there exists\"), \"for all\",\n      \"and\", \"or\", \"not\". If the existence of a set containing all the\n      specified elements is known (as is always the case in this\n      module), this is denoted B = {x : S(x)}.">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],

        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"strict">>]},
        <<" relation\n          corresponding to R. Conversely, if S is a relation in X, and if R is\n          defined so that x R y if x S y or x = y,\n          then R is the ">>,
        {<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"weak_relation">>}],[]},
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"weak">>]},
        <<"\n          relation corresponding to S.">>]},
      {<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"A relation R in X is ">>,
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"reflexive">>]},
        <<" if x R x for every\n          element x of X, it is ">>,
        {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"symmetric">>]},

The fact\n      that [{A,B}] matches the type of Arg1 is to be interpreted as\n      Arg1 representing a binary relation from X to Y, where X is\n      defined as all sets Set(x) for some element x in Sets the type\n      of which is A, and similarly for Y. In the same way Arg2 is\n      interpreted as representing a binary relation from W to Z.\n      Finally it is checked that B matches C, which is sufficient to\n      ensure that W is equal to Y. The untyped empty set is handled\n      separately: its type, ['_'], matches the type of any unordered\n      set.">>]},

        <<", Fun is\n          applied to the external set of each element of the given set and the\n          return value is assumed to be an external set. Selecting the\n          elements of an unordered set as external sets and assembling a\n          new unordered set from a list of external sets is in the present\n          implementation more efficient than modifying each element as a\n          set. However, this optimization can only be used when the\n          elements of the unordered set are atomic or ordered sets.      [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Specifying a SetFun as an integer I is equivalent to\n          specifying ">>,
        {<<"span">>,

 [{<<"p">>,[],

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The registry is a hierarchical database, used to store various system\n      and software information in Windows.\n      It contains installation data, and is updated by installers\n      and system programs. The Erlang installer updates the registry by adding\n      data that Erlang needs.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],

   [<<"Paths to keys are left to right, with subkeys to the right and backslash\n      between keys. (Remember that backslashes must be doubled in Erlang\n      strings.) Case is preserved but not significant.">>]},

   [<<"For example,\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
     [<<"\"\\\\hkey_local_machine\\\\software\\\\Ericsson\\\\Erlang\\\\5.0\"">>]},

   [{<<"pre">>,[],

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The following are some of the most important and attractive\n      capabilities provided by Mnesia:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"A relational/object hybrid data model that is suitable\n       for telecommunications applications.\n      ">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"A DBMS query language, Query List Comprehension (QLC) as\n       an add-on library.\n      ">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"Persistence. Tables can be coherently kept on disc and\n       in the main memory.\n      ">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"Replication. Tables can be replicated at several nodes.\n      ">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"Atomic transactions. A series of table manipulation\n       operations can be grouped into a single atomic transaction.\n      ">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"Location transparency. Programs can be written without\n       knowledge of the actual data location.\n      ">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],[<<"Extremely fast real-time data searches.\n      ">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"Schema manipulation routines. The DBMS can be\n       reconfigured at runtime without stopping the system.\n      ">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This Reference Manual describes the Mnesia API. This\n      includes functions that define and manipulate Mnesia\n      tables.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"All functions in this Reference Manual can be used in any\n      combination with queries using the list comprehension notation.\n      For information about the query notation, see the\n      ">>,
    {<<"span">>,

   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The first level is at the transport entry / exit point, i.e.\n          immediately after the receipt of the message before any message\n          processing is done (accept_recv) and \n          immediately before sending the message after all message\n          processing is done (accept_send).">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"The second level is at the MPD entry / exit point, i.e.\n          immediately after the basic message processing (accept_recv_pdu) / \n          immediately before the basic message processing (accept_send_pdu).">>]}]}]},

    <<" contains generic functions for \n    implementing tables (and variables) using the SNMP built-in database \n    or Mnesia. These default functions are used if no instrumentation \n    function is provided for a managed object in a MIB. Sometimes, \n    it might be necessary to customize the behaviour of the default \n    functions. For example, in some situations a trap should be sent \n    if a row is deleted or modified, or some hardware is to be informed, \n    when information is changed. ">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"The overall structure is shown in the following figure:">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"\n         +---------------+\n         |   SNMP Agent  |\n         +- - - - - - - -+\n         |      MIB      |\n         +---------------+\n                 |\n         Association file       (associates a MIB object with\n                 |               snmp_generic:table_funct\n                 |               snmp_generic:variable_func)\n+--------------------------------------+\n|           snmp_generic               |  Support for get-next,\n|                                      |  RowStatus operations\n+----------------------+---------------+\n|    snmpa_local_db    |    Mnesia     |  Database\n+--------------+-------+---------------+\n|     dets     |  ets  | \n| (persistent) |       | \n+--------------+-------+     ">>]}]},

    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Name">>]},

It is implemented as an ets\n      table of the ordered_set data-type, which means that all operations are\n      O(log n).  In the table, the key is an ASN.1 OBJECT\n      IDENTIFIER.\n      ">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This index is used to separate the implementation of the SNMP\n      ordering from the actual implementation of the table.  The SNMP\n      ordering, that is implementation of GET NEXT, is implemented in this\n      module.\n      ">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"For example, suppose there is an SNMP table, which is best\n      implemented in Erlang as one process per SNMP table row.  Suppose\n      further that the INDEX in the SNMP table is an OCTET STRING.  The\n      index structure would be created as follows:\n      ">>]},

   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"\nsnmp_index:new(string)\n    ">>]}]},

   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"With this structure, we can now map an OBJECT IDENTIFIER in\n      e.g. a GET NEXT request, to the correct process:\n      ">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"It also handles C-nodes, C-programs that talks erlang\n      distribution with erlang nodes (or other C-nodes) using the\n      erlang distribution format. The difference between ">>,

    <<" library is built on top of\n      ">>,

    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"ei">>]},

The index is updated to point right after the term\n      encoded/decoded. No checking is done whether the term fits in\n      the buffer or not. If encoding goes outside the buffer, the\n      program may crash.">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If the name after the prefix and any lift and glob markers is ">>,
