    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@@_">>]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@__">>]},
    <<", or even ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@__@_">>]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Finally, if the name without any prefixes or lift/glob markers begins with\n  an uppercase character, as in ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Foo">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@_@Foo">>]},
    <<", it will become a\n  variable on the Erlang level, and can be used to easily deconstruct and\n  construct syntax trees:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     case Input of\n         ?Q(\"{foo, _@Number}\") -> ?Q(\"foo:bar(_@Number)\");\n         ...">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  We refer to these as \"automatic metavariables\". If in addition the name ends\n  with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"@">>]},
    <<", as in ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Foo@">>]},
    <<", the value of the variable as an Erlang term will\n  be automatically converted to the corresponding abstract syntax tree when\n  used to construct a larger tree. For example, in:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     Bar = {bar, 42},\n     Foo = ?Q(\"{foo, _@Bar@}\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  (where Bar is just some term, not a syntax tree) the result ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Foo">>]},
    <<" will be a\n  syntax tree representing ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{foo, {bar, 42}}">>]},
    <<". This avoids the need for\n  temporary variables in order to inject data, as in\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     TmpBar = erl_syntax:abstract(Bar),\n     Foo = ?Q(\"{foo, _@TmpBar}\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If the context requires an integer rather than a variable, an atom, or a\n  string, you cannot use the uppercase convention to mark an automatic\n  metavariable. Instead, if the integer (without the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"909">>]},
    <<"-prefix and\n  lift/glob markers) ends in a ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"9">>]},
    <<", the integer will become an Erlang-level\n  variable prefixed with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Q">>]},
    <<", and if it ends with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"99">>]},
    <<" it will also be\n  automatically abstracted. For example, the following will increment the\n  arity of the exported function f:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     case Form of\n         ?Q(\"-export([f/90919]).\") ->\n             Q2 = erl_syntax:concrete(Q1) + 1,\n             ?Q(\"-export([f/909299]).\");\n         ...">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,
     [{<<"name">>,<<"When_to_use_the_various_forms_of_metavariables">>}],
     []},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"When to use the various forms of metavariables">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Merl can only parse a fragment of text if it follows the basic syntactical\n  rules of Erlang. In most places, a normal Erlang variable can be used as\n  metavariable, for example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"f(_@Arg)\") = Expr">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  but if you want to match on something like the name of a function, you have\n  to use an atom as metavariable:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"'@Name'() -> _@@_.\" = Function">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  (note the anonymous glob variable ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@@_">>]},
    <<" to ignore the function body).">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"In some contexts, only a string or an integer is allowed. For example, the\n  directive ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"-file(Name, Line)">>]},
    <<" requires that ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Name">>]},
    <<" is a string literal and\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Line">>]},
    <<" an integer literal:">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     ?Q(\"-file(\\\"'@File\\\", 9090).\") = ?Q(\"-file(\\\"foo.erl\\\", 42).\")).">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  This will extract the string literal ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"foo.erl\"">>]},
    <<" into the variable ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Foo">>]},
    <<".\n  Note the use of the anonymous variable ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"9090">>]},
    <<" to ignore the line number. To  \nmatch and also bind a metavariable that must be an integer literal, we can  \nuse the convention of ending the integer with a 9, turning it into a  \nQ-prefixed variable on the Erlang level (see the previous section).">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"Globs">>}],[]},{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Globs">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Whenever you want to match out a number of elements in a sequence (zero or\n  more) rather than a fixed set of elements, you need to use a glob. For\n  example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"{_@@Elements}\") = ?Q({a, b, c})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  will bind Elements to the list of individual syntax trees representing the\n  atoms ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"a">>]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"b">>]},
    <<", and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"c">>]},
    <<". This can also be used with static prefix and suffix\n  elements in the sequence. For example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     ?Q(\"{a, b, _@@Elements}\") = ?Q({a, b, c, d})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  will bind Elements to the list of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"c">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"d">>]},
    <<" subtrees, and\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     ?Q(\"{_@@Elements, c, d}\") = ?Q({a, b, c, d})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  will bind Elements to the list of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"a">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"b">>]},
    <<" subtrees. You can even use\n  plain metavariables in the prefix or suffix:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"{_@First, _@@Rest}\") = ?Q({a, b, c})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"\n  or\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"{_@@_, _@Last}\") = ?Q({a, b, c})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"  \n(ignoring all but the last element). You cannot however have two globs as  \npart of the same sequence.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"Lifted_metavariables">>}],[]},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Lifted metavariables">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"In some cases, the Erlang syntax rules make it impossible to place a\n  metavariable directly where you would like it. For example, you cannot\n  write:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"-export([_@@Name]).\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  to match out all name/arity pairs in the export list, or to insert a list of\n  exports in a declaration, because the Erlang parser only allows elements on\n  the form ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"A/I">>]},
    <<" (where ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"A">>]},
    <<" is an atom and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"I">>]},
    <<" an integer) in the export list.\n  A variable like the above is not allowed, but neither is a single atom or\n  integer, so ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@@Name'">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"909919">>]},
    <<" wouldn't work either.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"What you have to do in such cases is to write your metavariable in a\n  syntactically valid position, and use lifting markers to denote where it\n  should really apply, as in:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"-export(['@_@Name'/0]).\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  This causes the variable to be lifted (after parsing) to the next higher\n  level in the syntax tree, replacing that entire subtree. In this case, the\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@_@Name'/0">>]},
    <<" will be replaced with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@@Name'">>]},
    <<", and the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"/0">>]},
    <<"  \npart was just used as dummy notation and will be discarded.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"You may even need to apply lifting more than once. To match the entire\n  export list as a single syntax tree, you can write:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"-export(['@__Name'/0]).\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  using two underscores, but with no glob marker this time. This will make the\n  entire ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"['@__Name'/0]">>]},
    <<" part be replaced with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@Name'">>]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Sometimes, the tree structure of a code fragment isn't very obvious, and\n  parts of the structure may be invisible when printed as source code. For\n  instance, a simple function definition like the following:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     zero() -> 0.">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  consists of the name (the atom ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"zero">>]},
    <<"), and a list of clauses containing the\n  single clause ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"() -> 0">>]},
    <<". The clause consists of an argument list (empty), a\n  guard (empty), and a body (which is always a list of expressions) containing\n  the single expression ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"0">>]},
    <<". This means that to match out the name and the\n  list of clauses of any function, you'll need to use a pattern like\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
     [<<"?Q(\"'@Name'() -> _@_@Body.\")">>]},
    <<", using a dummy clause whose body is a glob  \nlifted one level.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"To visualize the structure of a syntax tree, you can use the function\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"merl:show(T)">>]},
    <<", which prints a summary. For example, entering\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     merl:show(merl:quote(\"inc(X, Y) when Y > 0 -> X + Y.\"))">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  in the Erlang shell will print the following (where the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"+">>]},
    <<" signs separate\n  groups of subtrees on the same level):\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     function: inc(X, Y) when ... -> X + Y.\n       atom: inc\n       +\n       clause: (X, Y) when ... -> X + Y\n         variable: X\n         variable: Y\n         +\n         disjunction: Y > 0\n           conjunction: Y > 0\n             infix_expr: Y > 0\n               variable: Y\n               +\n               operator: >\n               +\n               integer: 0\n         +\n         infix_expr: X + Y\n           variable: X\n           +\n           operator: +\n           +\n           variable: Y">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This shows another important non-obvious case: a clause guard, even if it's\n  as simple as ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Y > 0">>]},
    <<", always consists of a single disjunction of one or more\n  conjunctions of tests, much like a tuple of tuples. Thus:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will only match a guard with exactly one\n      test">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match a guard with one or more\n      comma-separated tests (but no semicolons), binding ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the list\n      of tests">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@_Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match just like the previous pattern, but\n      binds ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the conjunction subtree">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@_@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match an arbitrary nonempty guard,\n      binding ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the list of conjunction subtrees">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@__Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match like the previous pattern, but\n      binds ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the whole disjunction subtree">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"and finally, ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@__@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match any clause,\n      binding ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"[]">>]},
        <<" if the guard is empty and to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"[Disjunction]">>]},
        <<"\n      otherwise">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Thus, the following pattern matches all possible clauses:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     \"(_@Args) when _@__@Guard -> _@Body\"">>]}]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Parse transform for merl. Enables the use of automatic metavariables\n  and using quasi-quotes in matches and case switches. Also optimizes calls\n  to functions in ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"merl">>]},
    <<" by partially evaluating them, turning strings to  \ntemplates, etc., at compile-time.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],

    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"MERL_NO_TRANSFORM">>]},
    <<" is defined first.">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"A generic pretty printer library. This module uses a  \nstrict-style context passing implementation of John Hughes algorithm,  \ndescribed in \"The design of a Pretty-printing Library\".     {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],

    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#text-1">>}],[<<"text/1">>]}]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#above-2">>}],[<<"above/2">>]}]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,

    {<<"span">>,

  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If you simply want to format a paragraph of plain text, you probably\n  want to use the ">>,

     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#text_par-2">>}],[<<"text_par/2">>]}]},
    <<" function, as in the following\n  example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"  prettypr:format(prettypr:text_par(\"Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet\"), 20)">>]}]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"epp_dodger">>]},
    <<" - bypasses the Erlang preprocessor.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module tokenises and parses most Erlang source code without\n  expanding preprocessor directives and macro applications, as long as\n  these are syntactically \"well-behaved\". Because the normal parse\n  trees of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl_parse">>]},
    <<" module cannot represent these things\n  (normally, they are expanded by the Erlang preprocessor ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"epp.html">>}],[<<"epp(3)">>]}]},
    <<" before the parser sees them), an extended syntax tree\n  is created, using the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"erl_syntax.html">>}],[<<"erl_syntax">>]}]},
    <<" module.">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Functions for reading comment lines from Erlang source code.">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],[<<"Pretty printing of abstract Erlang syntax trees.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module is a front end to the pretty-printing library module\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"prettypr">>]},
    <<", for text formatting of abstract syntax trees defined by\n  the module ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl_syntax">>]},
    <<".">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],[<<"Inserting comments into abstract Erlang syntax trees">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module contains functions for inserting comments, described\n  by position, indentation and text, as attachments on an abstract\n  syntax tree, at the correct places.">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],[<<"Abstract Erlang syntax trees.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module defines an abstract data type for representing Erlang\n  source code as syntax trees, in a way that is backwards compatible\n  with the data structures created by the Erlang standard library\n  parser module ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl_parse">>]},
    <<" (often referred to as \"parse\n  trees\", which is a bit of a misnomer). This means that all\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl_parse">>]},
    <<" trees are valid abstract syntax trees, but the\n  reverse is not true: abstract syntax trees can in general not be used\n  as input to functions expecting an ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl_parse">>]},
    <<" tree.\n  However, as long as an abstract syntax tree represents a correct\n  Erlang program, the function ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#revert-1">>}],[<<"revert/1">>]}]},
    <<" should be able to\n  transform it to the corresponding ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl_parse">>]},
    <<"  \nrepresentation.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"A recommended starting point for the first-time user is the documentation\n  of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#type-syntaxTree">>}],[<<"syntaxTree()">>]}]},
    <<" data type, and the function ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],

   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"NOTES:">>}],[]},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"NOTES:">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This module deals with the composition and decomposition of\n  ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"syntactic">>]},
    <<" entities (as opposed to semantic ones); its  \npurpose is to hide all direct references to the data structures used  \nto represent these entities. With few exceptions, the functions in  \nthis module perform no semantic interpretation of their inputs, and  \nin general, the user is assumed to pass type-correct arguments - if  \nthis is not done, the effects are not defined.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"With the exception of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"#type-erl_parse">>}],[<<"erl_parse()">>]}]},
    <<" data structures,\n  the internal representations of abstract syntax trees are subject to\n  change without notice, and should not be documented outside this\n  module. Furthermore, we do not give any guarantees on how an abstract\n  syntax tree may or may not be represented, ">>,
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"with the following\n  exceptions">>]},
    <<": no syntax tree is represented by a single atom, such\n  as ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"none">>]},
    <<", by a list constructor ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"[X | Y]">>]},
    <<", or\n  by the empty list ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"[]">>]},
    <<". This can be relied on when writing\n  functions that operate on syntax trees.">>]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],[<<"Support library for abstract Erlang syntax trees.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],

 [{<<"p">>,[],

   [<<"Caveats: It is possible that in some intricate uses of macros,  \nthe automatic addition or removal of parentheses around uses or  \narguments could cause the resulting program to be rejected by the  \ncompiler; however, we have found no such case in existing  \ncode.  [{<<"p">>,[],[<<"Igor: the Module Merger and Renamer.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The program Igor merges the source code of one or more Erlang  \nmodules into a single module, which can then replace the original set  \nof modules. Igor is also able to rename a set of (possibly  \ninterdependent) modules, without joining them into a single  \nmodule.">>]},

       [<<"parse_transform/2">>]}]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"A note of warning: Igor cannot do anything about the case when the\n  name of a remote function is passed to the built-in functions\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"apply">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"spawn">>]},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"unless">>]},

     [<<"apply(lists, reverse, [Xs])">>]},

  {<<"p">>,[],

  {<<"p">>,[],

  {<<"p">>,[],

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Metaprogramming in Erlang.\n  Merl is a more user friendly interface to the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"erl_syntax">>]},
    <<" module, making\n  it easy both to build new ASTs from scratch and to\n  match and decompose existing ASTs. For details that are outside the scope\n  of Merl itself, please see the documentation of ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],
     [{<<"a">>,[{<<"href">>,<<"erl_syntax.html">>}],[<<"erl_syntax">>]}]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"Quick_start">>}],[]},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Quick start">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"To enable the full power of Merl, your module needs to include the Merl\n  header file:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     -include_lib(\"syntax_tools/include/merl.hrl\").">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Then, you can use the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q(Text)">>]},
    <<" macros in your code to create ASTs or match\n  on existing ASTs. For example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     Tuple = ?Q(\"{foo, 42}\"),\n     ?Q(\"{foo, _@Number}\") = Tuple,\n     Call = ?Q(\"foo:bar(_@Number)\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Calling ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"merl:print(Call)">>]},
    <<" will then print the following code:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     foo:bar(42)">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q">>]},
    <<" macros turn the quoted code fragments into ASTs, and lifts\n  metavariables such as ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Tuple">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Number">>]},
    <<" to the level of your Erlang\n  code, so you can use the corresponding Erlang variables ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Tuple">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Number">>]},
    <<"  \ndirectly. This is the most straightforward way to use Merl, and in many  \ncases it's all you need.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"You can even write case switches using ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q">>]},
    <<" macros as patterns. For example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     case AST of\n         ?Q(\"{foo, _@Foo}\") -> handle(Foo);\n         ?Q(\"{bar, _@Bar}\") when erl_syntax:is_integer(Bar) -> handle(Bar);\n         _ -> handle_default()\n     end">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"These case switches only allow ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q(...)">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_">>]},
    <<" as clause patterns, and the  \nguards may contain any expressions, not just Erlang guard expressions.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If the macro ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"MERL_NO_TRANSFORM">>]},
    <<" is defined before the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"merl.hrl">>]},
    <<" header\n  file is included, the parse transform used by Merl will be disabled, and in\n  that case, the match expressions ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q(...) = ...">>]},
    <<", case switches using\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q(...)">>]},
    <<" patterns, and automatic metavariables like ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Tuple">>]},
    <<" cannot be\n  used in your code, but the Merl macros and functions still work. To do\n  metavariable substitution, you need to use the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q(Text, Map)">>]},
    <<" macro, e.g.:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     Tuple = ?Q(\"{foo, _@bar, _@baz}\", [{bar, Bar}, {baz,Baz}])">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The text given to a ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"?Q(Text)">>]},
    <<" macro can be either a single string, or a\n  list of strings. The latter is useful when you need to split a long\n  expression over multiple lines, e.g.:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     ?Q([\"case _@Expr of\",\n         \"  {foo, X} -> f(X);\",\n         \"  {bar, X} -> g(X)\",\n         \"  _ -> h(X)\"\n         \"end\"])">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"  \nIf there is a syntax error somewhere in the text (like the missing semicolon  \nin the second clause above) this allows Merl to generate an error message  \npointing to the exact line in your source code. (Just remember to  \ncomma-separate the strings in the list, otherwise Erlang will concatenate  \nthe string fragments as if they were a single string.)">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"Metavariable_syntax">>}],[]},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Metavariable syntax">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"There are several ways to write a metavariable in your quoted code:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Atoms starting with ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"@">>]},
        <<", for example ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@foo'">>]},
        <<" or ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@Foo'">>]}]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Variables starting with ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@">>]},
        <<", for example ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@bar">>]},
        <<" or ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Bar">>]}]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Strings starting with ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"'@">>]},
        <<", for example ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"'@File\"">>]}]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"Integers starting with 909, for example ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"9091">>]},
        <<" or ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"909123">>]}]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  Following the prefix, one or more ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"0">>]},
    <<" characters may be used to\n  indicate \"lifting\" of the variable one or more levels, and after that, a ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"@">>]},
    <<"\n  or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"9">>]},
    <<" character indicates a glob metavariable (matching zero or more\n  elements in a sequence) rather than a normal metavariable. For example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@_foo'">>]},
        <<" is lifted one level, and ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@__foo">>]},
        <<" is lifted two\n        levels">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@@bar">>]},
        <<" is a glob variable, and ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@_@bar">>]},
        <<" is a lifted glob\n        variable">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"90901">>]},
        <<" is a lifted variable,">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"90991">>]},
        <<" is a glob variable, and ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"9090091">>]},
        <<"\n        is a glob variable lifted two levels">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  (Note that the last character in the name is never considered to be a lift\n  or glob marker, hence, ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@__">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"90900">>]},
    <<" are only lifted one level, not  \ntwo. Also note that globs only matter for matching; when doing  \nsubstitutions, a non-glob variable can be used to inject a sequence of  \nelements, and vice versa.)">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If the name after the prefix and any lift and glob markers is ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"0">>]},
    <<",\n  the variable is treated as an anonymous catch-all pattern in matches. For\n  example, ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@_">>]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@@_">>]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@__">>]},
    <<", or even ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@__@_">>]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Finally, if the name without any prefixes or lift/glob markers begins with\n  an uppercase character, as in ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Foo">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@_@Foo">>]},
    <<", it will become a\n  variable on the Erlang level, and can be used to easily deconstruct and\n  construct syntax trees:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     case Input of\n         ?Q(\"{foo, _@Number}\") -> ?Q(\"foo:bar(_@Number)\");\n         ...">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  We refer to these as \"automatic metavariables\". If in addition the name ends\n  with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"@">>]},
    <<", as in ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@Foo@">>]},
    <<", the value of the variable as an Erlang term will\n  be automatically converted to the corresponding abstract syntax tree when\n  used to construct a larger tree. For example, in:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     Bar = {bar, 42},\n     Foo = ?Q(\"{foo, _@Bar@}\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  (where Bar is just some term, not a syntax tree) the result ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Foo">>]},
    <<" will be a\n  syntax tree representing ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"{foo, {bar, 42}}">>]},
    <<". This avoids the need for\n  temporary variables in order to inject data, as in\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     TmpBar = erl_syntax:abstract(Bar),\n     Foo = ?Q(\"{foo, _@TmpBar}\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"If the context requires an integer rather than a variable, an atom, or a\n  string, you cannot use the uppercase convention to mark an automatic\n  metavariable. Instead, if the integer (without the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"909">>]},
    <<"-prefix and\n  lift/glob markers) ends in a ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"9">>]},
    <<", the integer will become an Erlang-level\n  variable prefixed with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Q">>]},
    <<", and if it ends with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"99">>]},
    <<" it will also be\n  automatically abstracted. For example, the following will increment the\n  arity of the exported function f:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     case Form of\n         ?Q(\"-export([f/90919]).\") ->\n             Q2 = erl_syntax:concrete(Q1) + 1,\n             ?Q(\"-export([f/909299]).\");\n         ...">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,
     [{<<"name">>,<<"When_to_use_the_various_forms_of_metavariables">>}],
     []},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"When to use the various forms of metavariables">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Merl can only parse a fragment of text if it follows the basic syntactical\n  rules of Erlang. In most places, a normal Erlang variable can be used as\n  metavariable, for example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"f(_@Arg)\") = Expr">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  but if you want to match on something like the name of a function, you have\n  to use an atom as metavariable:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"'@Name'() -> _@@_.\" = Function">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  (note the anonymous glob variable ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"_@@_">>]},
    <<" to ignore the function body).">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"In some contexts, only a string or an integer is allowed. For example, the\n  directive ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"-file(Name, Line)">>]},
    <<" requires that ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Name">>]},
    <<" is a string literal and\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Line">>]},
    <<" an integer literal:">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     ?Q(\"-file(\\\"'@File\\\", 9090).\") = ?Q(\"-file(\\\"foo.erl\\\", 42).\")).">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  This will extract the string literal ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"foo.erl\"">>]},
    <<" into the variable ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Foo">>]},
    <<".\n  Note the use of the anonymous variable ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"9090">>]},
    <<" to ignore the line number. To  \nmatch and also bind a metavariable that must be an integer literal, we can  \nuse the convention of ending the integer with a 9, turning it into a  \nQ-prefixed variable on the Erlang level (see the previous section).">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"Globs">>}],[]},{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Globs">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Whenever you want to match out a number of elements in a sequence (zero or\n  more) rather than a fixed set of elements, you need to use a glob. For\n  example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"{_@@Elements}\") = ?Q({a, b, c})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  will bind Elements to the list of individual syntax trees representing the\n  atoms ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"a">>]},
    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"b">>]},
    <<", and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"c">>]},
    <<". This can also be used with static prefix and suffix\n  elements in the sequence. For example:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     ?Q(\"{a, b, _@@Elements}\") = ?Q({a, b, c, d})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  will bind Elements to the list of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"c">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"d">>]},
    <<" subtrees, and\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     ?Q(\"{_@@Elements, c, d}\") = ?Q({a, b, c, d})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  will bind Elements to the list of the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"a">>]},
    <<" and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"b">>]},
    <<" subtrees. You can even use\n  plain metavariables in the prefix or suffix:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"{_@First, _@@Rest}\") = ?Q({a, b, c})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"\n  or\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"{_@@_, _@Last}\") = ?Q({a, b, c})">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"  \n(ignoring all but the last element). You cannot however have two globs as  \npart of the same sequence.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [{<<"a">>,[{<<"name">>,<<"Lifted_metavariables">>}],[]},
    {<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Lifted metavariables">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"In some cases, the Erlang syntax rules make it impossible to place a\n  metavariable directly where you would like it. For example, you cannot\n  write:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"-export([_@@Name]).\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  to match out all name/arity pairs in the export list, or to insert a list of\n  exports in a declaration, because the Erlang parser only allows elements on\n  the form ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"A/I">>]},
    <<" (where ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"A">>]},
    <<" is an atom and ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"I">>]},
    <<" an integer) in the export list.\n  A variable like the above is not allowed, but neither is a single atom or\n  integer, so ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@@Name'">>]},
    <<" or ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"909919">>]},
    <<" wouldn't work either.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"What you have to do in such cases is to write your metavariable in a\n  syntactically valid position, and use lifting markers to denote where it\n  should really apply, as in:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"-export(['@_@Name'/0]).\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  This causes the variable to be lifted (after parsing) to the next higher\n  level in the syntax tree, replacing that entire subtree. In this case, the\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@_@Name'/0">>]},
    <<" will be replaced with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@@Name'">>]},
    <<", and the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"/0">>]},
    <<"  \npart was just used as dummy notation and will be discarded.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"You may even need to apply lifting more than once. To match the entire\n  export list as a single syntax tree, you can write:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     ?Q(\"-export(['@__Name'/0]).\")">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  using two underscores, but with no glob marker this time. This will make the\n  entire ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"['@__Name'/0]">>]},
    <<" part be replaced with ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"'@Name'">>]},
    <<".">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Sometimes, the tree structure of a code fragment isn't very obvious, and\n  parts of the structure may be invisible when printed as source code. For\n  instance, a simple function definition like the following:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     zero() -> 0.">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  consists of the name (the atom ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"zero">>]},
    <<"), and a list of clauses containing the\n  single clause ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"() -> 0">>]},
    <<". The clause consists of an argument list (empty), a\n  guard (empty), and a body (which is always a list of expressions) containing\n  the single expression ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"0">>]},
    <<". This means that to match out the name and the\n  list of clauses of any function, you'll need to use a pattern like\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
     [<<"?Q(\"'@Name'() -> _@_@Body.\")">>]},
    <<", using a dummy clause whose body is a glob  \nlifted one level.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"To visualize the structure of a syntax tree, you can use the function\n  ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"merl:show(T)">>]},
    <<", which prints a summary. For example, entering\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     merl:show(merl:quote(\"inc(X, Y) when Y > 0 -> X + Y.\"))">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"\n  in the Erlang shell will print the following (where the ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"+">>]},
    <<" signs separate\n  groups of subtrees on the same level):\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],
     [<<"     function: inc(X, Y) when ... -> X + Y.\n       atom: inc\n       +\n       clause: (X, Y) when ... -> X + Y\n         variable: X\n         variable: Y\n         +\n         disjunction: Y > 0\n           conjunction: Y > 0\n             infix_expr: Y > 0\n               variable: Y\n               +\n               operator: >\n               +\n               integer: 0\n         +\n         infix_expr: X + Y\n           variable: X\n           +\n           operator: +\n           +\n           variable: Y">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"This shows another important non-obvious case: a clause guard, even if it's\n  as simple as ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Y > 0">>]},
    <<", always consists of a single disjunction of one or more\n  conjunctions of tests, much like a tuple of tuples. Thus:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will only match a guard with exactly one\n      test">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match a guard with one or more\n      comma-separated tests (but no semicolons), binding ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the list\n      of tests">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@_Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match just like the previous pattern, but\n      binds ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the conjunction subtree">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@_@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match an arbitrary nonempty guard,\n      binding ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the list of conjunction subtrees">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [{<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@__Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match like the previous pattern, but\n      binds ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to the whole disjunction subtree">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"p">>,[],
       [<<"and finally, ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"\"when _@__@Guard ->\"">>]},
        <<" will match any clause,\n      binding ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Guard">>]},
        <<" to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"[]">>]},
        <<" if the guard is empty and to ">>,
        {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"[Disjunction]">>]},
        <<"\n      otherwise">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Thus, the following pattern matches all possible clauses:\n  ">>]},
  {<<"div">>,
   [{<<"class">>,<<"example">>}],
   [{<<"pre">>,[],[<<"     \"(_@Args) when _@__@Guard -> _@Body\"">>]}]}],
 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Parse transform for merl. Enables the use of automatic metavariables\n  and using quasi-quotes in matches and case switches. Also optimizes calls\n  to functions in ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"merl">>]},

    <<" is defined first.">>]}],

    <<", ">>,
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"bold_code">>}],

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"The event service defines two roles for objects: the supplier role and \n      the consumer role. Suppliers supply event data to the event channel and \n      consumers receive event data from the channel. Suppliers do not need to \n      know the identity of the consumers, and vice versa. Consumers and \n      suppliers are connected to the event channel via proxies, which are managed\n      by ConsumerAdmin and SupplierAdmin objects.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"There are four general models of communication.  These are:    ">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"The canonical push model. It allows the suppliers of events to initiate the\n       transfer of event data to consumers. Event channels play the role of \n      ">>,
      {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Notifier">>]},
      <<". Active suppliers use event channel to push data to \n       passive consumers registered with the event channel.">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"The canonical pull model. It allows consumers to request events from \n       suppliers. Event channels play the role of ">>,
      {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Procure">>]},
      <<" since they \n       procure events on behalf of consumers. Active consumers can explicitly \n       pull data from passive suppliers via the event channels.">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"The hybrid push/pull model. It allows consumers request events queued at\n       a channel by suppliers. Event channels play the role of ">>,
      {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Queue">>]},
      <<".\n       Active consumers explicitly pull data deposited by active suppliers via \n       the event channels.">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [<<"The hybrid pull/push model. It allows the channel to pull events from \n       suppliers and push them to consumers. Event channels play the role of \n      ">>,
      {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"Intelligent agent">>]},
      <<". Active event channels can pull data from \n       passive suppliers to push it to passive consumers.">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"To get access to all definitions, e.g., exceptions,\n      include necessary ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"hrl">>]},
    <<" files by using:">>,
    {<<"br">>,[],[]},
    {<<"span">>,
     [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
     [<<"-include_lib(\"cosEvent/include/*.hrl\").">>]}]},

 [{<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"An event channel is an object that allows multiple suppliers to communicate\n      with multiple consumers in a highly decoupled, asynchronous manner. The event \n      channel is built up incrementally. When an event channel is\n      created no suppliers or consumers are connected to it. Event Channel can\n      implement group communication by serving as a replicator, broadcaster, or\n      multicaster that forward events from one or more suppliers to multiple\n      consumers.">>]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"It is up to the user to decide when an event channel is created and how \n      references to the event channel are obtained.      [<<"Value - integer(), range (31 digits): ±9999999999999999999999999999999">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"Since the Value part is represented by an integer, it is vital that the\n      Digits and Scale values are correct. This also means that trailing zeros\n      cannot be left out in some cases:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],[<<"fixed<5,3> eq. 03.140d eq. 3140">>]},
    {<<"li">>,[],[<<"fixed<3,2> eq. 3.14d eq. 314">>]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],[<<"Leading zeros can be left out.">>]},

   [<<"For your convenience, this module exports functions which handle\n      unary (">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"-">>]},
    <<") and binary (">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"+-*/">>]},
    <<") operations legal for the Fixed type.\n      Since a unary ">>,
    {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"+">>]},
    <<" have no effect, this module do not export such a \n      function. Any of the binary operations may cause an overflow (i.e. more than\n      31 significant digits; leading and trailing zeros are not considered \n      significant). If this is the case, the Digit and Scale values are adjusted\n      and the Value truncated (no rounding performed). This behavior is\n      compliant with the OMG CORBA specification. Each binary operation have\n      the following upper bounds:">>]},
  {<<"ul">>,[],
   [{<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Fixed1 + Fixed2">>]},

       [<<"fixed<max(d1-s1,d2-s2) + max(s1,s2) + 1, max(s1,s2)>">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Fixed1 - Fixed2">>]},

      {<<"span">>,
       [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
       [<<"fixed<max(d1-s1,d2-s2) + max(s1,s2) + 1, max(s1,s2)>">>]}]},

     [{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Fixed1 * Fixed2">>]},

      {<<"span">>,[{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],[<<"fixed<d1+d2, s1+s2>">>]}]},
    {<<"li">>,[],
     [{<<"strong">>,[],[<<"Fixed1 / Fixed2">>]},
      <<" - ">>,
      {<<"span">>,
       [{<<"class">>,<<"code">>}],
       [<<"fixed<(d1-s1+s2) + Sinf ,Sinf >">>]}]}]},
  {<<"p">>,[],
   [<<"A quotient may have an arbitrary number of decimal places, which is \n      denoted by a scale of Sinf.">>]}],
